<div id="review_445697938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445697938" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445697938?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=romantica-or-erotica">romantica-or-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=menage">menage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=bdsm-or-person-in-control">bdsm-or-person-in-control</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445697938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4514180179023633648"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380396082i/763234.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>We've come full circle...</b><br/><br/>...and so I will now go back to my rating for book 1. Books 2 and 3 were wonderfully dark and fluid reads, which were book-ended by a series beginning and ending that were knitted together to form a continuous entity.<br/><br/>The Original Sinners series is definitely different. It's going to push you out of your comfort zone. I remember reading the first book and feeling unsure how to feel about this journey that I'd started. Then I read books 2 and 3 and couldn't put them down. </span>
  <span id="freeText4514180179023633648" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380396082i/763234.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>We've come full circle...</b><br><br>...and so I will now go back to my rating for book 1. Books 2 and 3 were wonderfully dark and fluid reads, which were book-ended by a series beginning and ending that were knitted together to form a continuous entity.<br><br>The Original Sinners series is definitely different. It's going to push you out of your comfort zone. I remember reading the first book and feeling unsure how to feel about this journey that I'd started. Then I read books 2 and 3 and couldn't put them down. Who knew that I'd come to fall for a set of darkly twisted individuals? Whatever it is that's going on here, surely there's some voodoo magic involved because I kept wanting to know more.<br><br>This is not really a review, but more a long ramble of my thoughts. I had quotes but decided to just free form this. Potential mild spoilers ahead if you haven't read up through book 3 of the series.<br><br><b>First, a few smallish complaints</b>.<br><br>~ I could have done without Zach and Grace in this series. The story would have stood on its own without their presence. Grace as a pal for Nora? Uh, okay. That situation felt too forced, as if we were being coerced into believing these two women fell so easily into a friendship. Grace exploring her sexuality without Zach? Again I say...uh, okay. I could honestly care less.<br><br>As much as I wanted other women in this series to take some of the worship away from Nora and her magical vagina (dude, even the book said so, which made me laugh hard), I didn't think bringing Grace in for the final book was the solution. Her part in the story felt completely tacked on, almost as if it needed to be there in order to justify why Zach was a character in book 1.<br><br>~ Going to go ahead and tag my usual (yes, I seem to have one every review, so most of this isn't new) Nora rant, so if you'd prefer not to read my Nora frustrations, don't click this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's no secret that I've never been a fan of Nora. I still feel like after 4 books that I know nothing about her other than everything she does and thinks about is tied to sex, even her job as an author and the friendships that she keeps. WHO is she as a person, outside of her sexual identity? Before you hit me with the obvious answer that this is erotica, let me riddle you this : We know all about who Soren is with his faith and calling, and who Wesley is and wants to be - and what moves them. Why didn't we get to know more about Nora, other than a laundry list of what makes her appealing to other people (most of it physical or aesthetic/presentation in nature, such as her infectious laugh). Even in the most sexually-free environment, there has to be more about a person which shapes them than their desire to be poly-amorous and have sex whenever and however it suits them. It's perfectly (and I truly mean this) fine that she's not going to be a married mom living in suburbia, but I felt like I never really got to know her outside of her surface personality-traits and looks. What about hobbies, goals, future plans, etc? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'm actually a bigger fan of young Eleanor. She liked to steal cars (hey at least she had one non-sexual hobby). The upcoming White Years series looks like it will be interesting, as we will be traveling back in time to life before the Original Sinners.<br><br>~ The entire kidnap portion of the story served as a vehicle for flashbacks, a few of which I skimmed. I can't put my finger on it, but something just didn't hold my interest with this book the way I was glued to the pages with books 2 and 3. <br><br><b>But let's get back to the goodness, shall we?</b><br><br>~ As usual, the Wes part of the story was the big highlight for me. Soren only gets yummier and yummier. Soren plus Wes in the same room = entertaining.<br><br>~ The Griffin and Michael interlude gets two very enthusiastic thumbs up!<br><br>~ I liked the addition of Soren's niece. She was cute and I was a big fan of the role she played in the story.<br><br>~ Nora did have a great scene near the end with Soren. I can't spoil it, but she was awesome with what she did. I thought it felt like one of those "long time coming" situations.<br><br><b>The negative in this review probably makes it look like I didn't care for the book, which isn't true.</b> I loved many of the character interactions and the sex scenes never disappointed. I do wish that the amount of flashbacks were scaled down because those dragged the story out to the point where I was thinking that at least a couple of the non-pivotal recollections could have been saved for another book. <br><br><i>The Mistress</i> wasn't a bad series ender, but it wasn't on par with the previous book in the series. I'll be rating this as a marginal success - definitely worth the read for sure, and I'm thankful for the fair amount of closure that we got. I would still recommend it for anyone looking to dabble in the realm of dark erotica. You won't find many authors out there who are able to seamlessly intermingle eroticism with a clever literary style the way Ms. Reisz can. <br><br><i>This book provided from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4514180179023633648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_460849941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460849941" />
    <a title="Mimi Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4884889-mimi-smith"><img alt="Mimi Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297016674p2/4884889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460849941?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Smith" href="/user/show/4884889-mimi-smith">Mimi Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4884889-mimi-smith?shelf=r">r</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460849941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10134459772080414253"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>First of all-do NOT read these books out of order. There's no point. If you are reading this review prepare to be spoiled about the rest of the series. I'll spoiler tag anything that is a spoiler to this book.<br/><br/>After weeks of stalling I finally decided writing this review is not gonna get any easier. High expectations are a bitch. And so many conflicting emotions an even bigger one. But if I'm to untangle all that I felt about this book, I'm going to have to go one step at the time...Like</span>
  <span id="freeText10134459772080414253" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />First of all-do NOT read these books out of order. There's no point. If you are reading this review prepare to be spoiled about the rest of the series. I'll spoiler tag anything that is a spoiler to this book.<br /><br />After weeks of stalling I finally decided writing this review is not gonna get any easier. High expectations are a bitch. And so many conflicting emotions an even bigger one. But if I'm to untangle all that I felt about this book, I'm going to have to go one step at the time...Like in the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Queen</u>
</b><br /><br />AKA - The Mistress. Nora is right where we left her. Or near enough. She's been kidnapped by Marie-Laurie the crazy ho. Seems like Kingsley's sister and Soren's wife has always been a psycho and now she's back for some kind of revenge. Nora's in a bind, so to speak. But she still has her words and although she doesn't want to give Marie-Laurie precious bits of herself and the men she loves, she'll use her words, he stories, her wild past to prolong this and save herself. <br /><br />There's a lot of backtracking in this one. We see the past through Nora's eyes, and I can see the necessity-we need to see how and why she makes the choices that she does - but I still would have loved more of the present. There was one menage scene that was *gulp*. I went a little blind there, I think. <br /><br />And you know what: I finally completely like Nora. She's so free in her skin, her choices, her love. She's unrestrained. And don't we all wish to be, deep down? I also feel she made the only choice she could have, should have to keep true to herself.<br /><br /><i>“Love versus love. King, you’re comparing infinities. There is no ‘more.’ That’s not how love works. If it’s love, it’s infinite. You can’t count it."</i><br /><br />How true. You don't love someone "more". You love them differently. Although, just from a mathematical viewpoint, some infinities are larger than others. Just sayin'.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The King</u>
</b><br /><br />Ah, Kingsley.... Je t'aime. He and Nora really are kindred spirits. He's just as wild and unpredictable. Wholly his own person, he does what he wants and live that way as well. Now he's facing a difficult situation to say the least. His sister is...alive. He's blamed himself for her death for thirty years and she's alive. And now he might have to kill her to save Nora, whom he loves and hates, but is his family in truth. He's heading to them, both of them to resolve it all... After tying up Soren, of course (for his own good!)<br /><br /><i>Wesley’s eyes widened when he took in the scene. On the floor, at the end of the biggest red bed he’d ever seen in his life, sat Søren, his blond head bowed, his eyes closed. “Talk away. He may not talk back, however.”<br />“What the hell…?”<br />“He threatened to call the police,” Kingsley said matter-of-factly. “The police, the church and all city, state and federal authorities. I couldn’t allow that. For his sake.”<br />“So you…”<br />“Sedated him. And handcuffed him. He’ll be out another hour at least with the shot I gave him.”<br />“You drugged Søren?”<br /><br />“I’m a pacifist. I don’t believe nonconsensual violence is ever justified. I am trying to remember that I’m a pacifist so I don’t murder Kingsley where he stands.”</i><br /><br />Just to think, such great conflict. Together with the place King and Soren's relationship was left in The Prince, it could've been so good... Sadly, we don't see much of King. I wanted more! It could've been awesome. <br /><br />*Sigh*. Oh, well, it is what it is. I am satisfied with the way things were left with him. Ecstatic, even :)<br /><br />I love, LOVE this scene.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“‘Jacob have I loved,’” Kingsley said in English once more. “‘Esau have I hated.’ Romans 9:13. I paid attention in school sometimes.”<br />“Not nearly enough attention.”<br />“I was preoccupied.”<br />“Obviously. You learned all the wrong verses. First Samuel 18:1. ‘And it came to pass, when he had made an end of speaking unto Saul, that the soul of Jonathan was knit with the soul of David, and Jonathan loved him as his own soul.’ First Samuel 20:16-17. ‘So Jonathan made a covenant with the house of David, saying, “Let the Lord even require it at the hands of David’s enemies.” And Jonathan caused David to swear again, because he loved him: for he loved as he loved his own soul.’ Second Samuel 1:26. ‘I am distressed for thee, my brother Jonathan…thy love to me was wonderful, passing the love of women.’”<br />Kingsley stared at Søren and found he couldn’t speak.<br />Søren smiled at his sudden muteness.<br />“Don’t get into a scriptural pissing contest with a Jesuit priest, Kingsley,” Søren chided. “You’ll lose every time.” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />An, just LOL. Who can come up with this, but the King:<br /><br /><i>“Our Nora has a magic pussy. It’s the opposite of the Bermuda Triangle. Lost men sail into it and then find themselves.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Knight</u>
</b><br /><br />Oh, Wes. If I met you in real life, I would probably jump on you and never let go... Here, though...<br /><br />Wes is lost. He just proposed to Nora (and she said yes!) and then someone took her away. This is not something he's used to. He doesn't know what to do. He's just afraid and forced to interact with all the other men in her life. He just can't fit Soren and Kingsley with his version of reality and right vs. wrong. Men don't hit women. Yet, these do. Even though it's consensual, he just can't accept it. <br /><br />He's doing some soul-searching, too. Someone helps him deal with the situation.<br /><br />In any case, I barely stopped myself from skipping his scenes. I like him, I swear! It's just in the company of such vivid and outrageous characters, when kidnappings and whatnot are happening, he's...normal. And I understand the need for that, but... *shrug*. That's just me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Pawn</u>
</b><br /><br />Laila, Soren's niece, is introduced here for the first time, with reason. I won't say anything more, because anything is a spoiler. She's nice and bubbly, though. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Rook</u>
</b><br /><br />Grace... I really don't get the need for this storyline in this book. It's not that I hate Grace or anything, it's just: I'm not a fan of where this all went. While reading, I was just thrown from one extreme to the other. This culminated in the very ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why, why, why did Soren sleep with her?? I thought he only did that with people he loved. And why would she want to be the submissive, hurt and all. Yes, I get it, to earn "it". But c'mon! And the baby! Still don't know how to feel about the baby... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. In the end, I can accept everything (reluctantly, but I can). But, again-necessity? Those things felt out of character to me. I would've far preferred to see more of the "after". Something not in the past, simply about my favorite characters. There's apparently some connection to the bible, but...again.<br /><br />After thinking about it a bit, I did see that Grace was the character through which we got to see Soren, his secrets and feelings, unbiased, since we'll never have his POV. But, still. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Religion</u>
</b><br /><br />I have to say this. I know many people won't read this because they are religious and the whole Soren's a priest thing is very unnerving. But it is NOT written for shock value or to besmirch faith in any way. In fact, Ms. Reisz is and has always been a believer.<br /><br />I'm an atheist. And as hard as it is to believe, these books showed me a more beautiful side of faith than I have ever seen before. Is it a contradiction? Yes, but there it is. There is a quote in The Prince, and I now know the feeling.<br /><br /><i>“Theresa of Avila…she wrote once that she didn’t love God <br />and didn’t want to love God, but she wanted to want to love <br />God.”</i> <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Fin</u>
</b><br /><br />You know, I'll always love Tiffany Reisz. She writes beautifully, with such vivid colors and strong emotions. She creates characters I love and worry over. Obsess over, even. They are real and fallible and amazing. You can see the strings and knots of love all connecting them. Here I wasn't a fan of some events and decisions, but that doesn't mean I don't remain a fan of TR. After all... I did read this book and couldn't stop till I was done, at about 4 am or something. And I would really want to see what happens next for these characters. After finishing, I was sure there was something I was missing. An epilogue or something, because I was in shock. But, no. And maybe that was how TR wanted to finish it, with everyone feeling strongly and wanting more. Still... Pretty please? <br /><br /> I look forward to The Priest. C'mon, imagine younger Nora exasperating Soren. Love it!<br /><br /><i>“You call her Little One?”<br />“I always have. She was a teenager when we met. A very ill-mannered teenager. She demanded to know why I was so tall. She insinuated I had grown this tall simply for attention.”<br /><br />“I explained to her that I was tall so I could hear God’s voice better. And since I was taller and could hear Him better, she should always listen to me. That didn’t sit very well with her. She retorted the next day with a verse from Psalm 114. ‘The Lord keeps the little ones.’ Her biblical proof that God prefers short people. I started calling her Little One after that. It helped us both remember she belonged to God first.”</i><br /><br /><b>ETA</b> I have no idea how I missed this the first time I read it, but knowing the ending it makes a lot of sense and is kind of awwww.<br /><br /><i>“Will I be a hero in your stories? Or the villain?”<br />“Haven’t decided yet,” Nora confessed. “But I promise you this…I will give you the last laugh.”<br />“Then that’s all I can ask.”<br />“And after I give you the last laugh, I’ll put my pen away and I’ll fall asleep. And when I wake up, you and I will be back together. I’ll be fifteen again and you’ll be twenty-nine and it will all start over again—you and I. That’s how I’ll know I’m in heaven.”</i><br /><br />And so came about, "The Saint", LOL.<br /><br /> <br /><i>
  <b>I spoiler-tagged all the info I gathered about the book and posted here before reading it below. </b>
</i> <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Coming Summer 2013</b><br /><br />-----4/23/2013------<br /><br />Teasers for The Mistress and the Mistress files <a href="http://us6.campaign-archive1.com/?u=955464b770&amp;id=be18af6cad" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br /><br />------Updated 2/3/2013-------<br /><br />Two more things. Well three if you count reassurances :) <br /><br /><i>"You will looooooooooove the ending. I think. I love it. Made me want to do cartwheels."<br /><br />#1-Two ppl you never imagined get together get together. <br />#2-Someone from Nora's past shows up.<br /><br />-TR</i><br /><br />----------------<br /><br />From the Goddess herself: <b> HINTS, TEASERS &amp; SPOILERS</b><br /><br />Not a day passes online that one of my readers doesn't call me a sadist. Some writers might take this as an insult, but in the world of The Original Sinners, it's something of a compliment. Even if it wasn't I could hardly argue. I left my readers at the end of The Prince (book three in the series) with a nasty cliffhanger. My leading lady, Mistress Nora Sutherlin, is gone. Poof. Vanished. All that we know is someone from Kingsley and Søren's past is involved, someone with a grudge. <br /><br />Like Søren, I wear my sadist badge proudly. I knew from the moment I started plotting all the books in the series that book three would end with the proverbial excrement hitting the metaphorical oscillator. I have a Dominatrix for a leading lady. She's tough as nails, funny and fearless, and almost congenitally incapable of settling down with just one man and behaving herself for more than five minutes at a time. But it's easy to be funny and fearless when your only opponents are a grumpy editor or a nosy reporter. I wanted to see how tough my Nora really is. I wanted her to face real danger, real mortal peril and see how she took it. For years now she's been dishing out the pain. I wanted to see how well she could take it.<br /><br />In book four, The Mistress, Nora awakes and finds herself in the clutches of an old enemy who is holding her hostage. Nora knows she has to give her captors a reason to keep her alive. She buys time by telling stories, turning into a modern-day Scheherazade. Unlike Scheherazade, however, Nora's stories are true, not legends. When interrogated over the supposed sins of her past, Nora spins erotic tales of the most important men in her life — Wesley, Kingsley, and Søren — and the passionate nights she spent with them.<br /><br />In story number one, she is forced to explain why she loves Wesley, a young man so entirely different from her and her world. In her second story, she reveals a dark secret about Kingsley and then tells her captor something about Søren even Kingsley doesn't know. In her final story, she explains the origin of her most precious possession, an item her captor threatens to burn if Nora can't choose once and for all who she loves more — Søren or Wesley. The stories buy her would-be rescuers desperately needed time. And when Kingsley overhears one of her stories while he's trying to save her, everything he thought he knew about love is called into question.<br /><br />In book one, The Siren, Nora's writing comes between her and the men she loves. In book four, The Mistress, Nora's way with words might be the only thing between her and certain death. <br /><br /><i>"Tell me a story."<br /><br />"You're going to have to talk to my agent," Nora said. "She handles all the book deals."<br /><br />"Damon?"<br /><br />Damon stepped forward again, knife at the ready.<br /><br />"Once upon a time," Nora began...<br /><br />- Tiffany Reisz</i><br /><br />___________________________________________________<br /><br /><br /><br />Release date July 30th. Available for pre-order as of now.<br /><br />Oh, and there's a synopsis:<br /><br /><i>Nora Sutherlin is being held, bound and naked. Under different circumstances, she would enjoy the situation immensely, but her captor isn't interested in play. Or pity. <br /><br />As the reality of her impending peril unfolds, Nora becomes Scheherazade, buying each hour of her life with stories-sensual tales of Søren, Kingsley and Wesley, each of whom has tempted and tested and tortured her in his own way. This, Nora realizes, is her life: nothing so simple, so vanilla, as a mere love triangle for her. It's a knot in a silken cord, a tangled mass of longings of the body and the heart and the mind. And it may unravel at any moment. <br /><br />But in Nora's world, no one is ever truly powerless-a cadre of her friends, protectors and lovers stands ready to do anything to save her, even when the only certainty seems to be sacrifice and heartbreak.... </i><br /><br />What, what, what does that mean?????<br /><br />Scheherazade? I don't mind the sensual stories, or the flashbacks, most likely, and we'll probably travel through those, and the boys' point of view, as Nora figures out where her future lies through her past, and is eventually rescued. that's just my thought on this.<br /><br />----------------<br />Which is forever away, right? Especially since the book is done and in the hands of editors and publishers.<br /><br />Anyhow, because after The Prince I became all obsessed about what could happen and what the future brings, not to mention I'm in lust with many of the characters, I started following (*cough* stalking *cough*) Mistress Reisz on Twitter in the hopes of finding out some tidbits. Since the aforementioned Goddess is very active there, here's some info about the upcoming book ant the Sinners in general. It's all jumbled up and if you conclude something useful, you're a rock star!<br /><br />- Grace will become a main character, because she has something to say and she does it in Welsh<br />- Another main character will be introduced<br />- There was a good reason Soren held his distance from King and we find it out here<br />- This book will be full of "mind fucks", twists and emotions<br />- Soren apparently becomes chattier here, and we'll learn more about the person who taught him how to be a dominant, as well as about his mother.<br />- Kingsley and Nora are a bit like siblings. They love each other, hate each other, fight and make up-only not quite as siblings, oui?<br />- Juliette and Soren are the only two loves of Kingsley's life and we'll find out more about her in The King<br />- Soren's safe word is Eleanor not because he needs it, but because she makes him feel safe<br />- The ending will be a cause for cartwheels, firework and celebration, so HEA, only we don't know in which form<br />- To all concerns expressed by the fans about Wes/Soren/Nora/Kingsley, Ms Reisz replies: Don't worry. I've got this, which means probably no one dies<br />- Soren will never stop being a priest and Wes will never be kinky.<br />- Nora will never have babies, just not who she is<br />- Nora'd be unhappy if she lived straightly vanilla, bc Nora is many things but vanilla isn't one of them.<br />"But Nora's not vanilla. Wes would never hurt her which is a nightmare for a kinky woman."<br />Wes: "I think that's the attraction for Nora. He's not in her intense world. He's a vacation from it."<br />-"You can't even begin to guess what I do with Wes, Nora, and Soren so don't even try."<br />- Oh, and not all is what it seems so far. And that final scene-with the proposal, something was going down then we knew nothing about but we'll learn what.<br />-"NOTHING is coincidence. Zach being Jewish isn't even a coincidence. That will mean something eventually."<br />-" He had said things to hurt Kingsley, why not admit it? *that what King said hurt him* It IS a great question that gets answered in book 4."<br />-"All priests are sexual beings with desires and sexual feelings. Soren had every intention of being celibate. He can be a celibate sadist. He fell in love and that changed everything,"<br />-No Soren POV. Ever.<br />-Griff and Mick will have more novellas later on.<br /><br /><b>Fear not! I have an equally awesome series planned.<br />It's contemporary urban fantasy. One of the main characters is the devil. He wears guyliner. He's like a male unfiltered Nora. Yes, he makes Nora look like a saint.</b>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Oh, and The Priest will probably be out in <b>early 2014.</b> <br /><br /><i>ARC received from Harlequin via Netgalley</i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18270788-the-mistress">review of another edition</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5029707397394537787"><b>***5 CHECKMATE Stars***</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Chess is a beautiful Mistress</i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426369i/851968.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As a lover and player of chess I thought <b> Ms. Reisz </b>did a brilliant job with her chess metaphors. I spent a lot of time thinking about each chess move and the players! <br/><br/>The story picks up right where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704485.The_Prince__The_Original_Sinners___3_' title='The Prince (The Original Sinners, #3) by Tiffany Reisz' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Prince</a> left us hanging. We know Nora's been kidnapped by Marie-Laure. <br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I gave them my death as a gift...and now I'm taking my gift back."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>All of our favorite characters from the three previous books return along with one character</span>
  <span id="freeText5029707397394537787" style="display:none"><b>***5 CHECKMATE Stars***</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Chess is a beautiful Mistress</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426369i/851968.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As a lover and player of chess I thought <b> Ms. Reisz </b>did a brilliant job with her chess metaphors. I spent a lot of time thinking about each chess move and the players! <br><br>The story picks up right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704485.The_Prince__The_Original_Sinners___3_" title="The Prince (The Original Sinners, #3) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prince</a> left us hanging. We know Nora's been kidnapped by Marie-Laure. <br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I gave them my death as a gift...and now I'm taking my gift back."</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>All of our favorite characters from the three previous books return along with one character from a novella. They are all involved in this game of chess. Each has a role to fulfill. <br><br><b>Which Queen will win? The White Queen or the Black Queen?</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426369i/851969._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>In the game of chess; the <b>Queen</b><i> protects her</i><b> King.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I'm Team Wesley and the chapter <b>PROMOTION </b>was well done. *don't read until you finished the book* <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i> A Promotion in Chess is when a pawn makes it across the board and then can be made into any piece. </i><br><b>Every Pawn can become a Queen!</b> And that is exactly what Laila did with Wesley. She will become the Queen of Kentucky.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The ending has left me speculating! I do know one thing for sure that <b>Ms. Reisz</b> is like our beloved, Soren- a sadist!<br><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10970532.The_Siren__The_Original_Sinners___1_" title="The Siren (The Original Sinners, #1) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1335832751s/10970532.jpg" alt="The Siren (The Original Sinners, #1) by Tiffany Reisz" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13548075.The_Angel__The_Original_Sinners___2_" title="The Angel (The Original Sinners, #2) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1337044736s/13548075.jpg" alt="The Angel (The Original Sinners, #2) by Tiffany Reisz" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704485.The_Prince__The_Original_Sinners___3_" title="The Prince (The Original Sinners, #3) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1344776840s/15704485.jpg" alt="The Prince (The Original Sinners, #3) by Tiffany Reisz" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17251444.The_Mistress__The_Original_Sinners___4_" title="The Mistress (The Original Sinners, #4) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1358807432s/17251444.jpg" alt="The Mistress (The Original Sinners, #4) by Tiffany Reisz" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Must be read in order. Big cliffhanger in book 3. Series is complete.<br><br>**ARC courtesy of Harlequin via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.**<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1896017682" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896017682" />
    <a title="Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3161105-maida---v--"><img alt="Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555353893p2/3161105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896017682?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»" href="/user/show/3161105-maida---v--">Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=mini-review">mini-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=paperback-or-hc-i-own">paperback-or-hc-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=bdsm">bdsm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=delicious-men">delicious-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=author-i-lurve">author-i-lurve</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3161105-maida---v--?shelf=books-of-2017">books-of-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896017682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17935421455497494170"><b>RATING: 4 Forever. Everything. Hearts!! <3</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Søren couldn’t live in a world without Nora. Kingsley couldn’t live in a world without Søren. Her death would be like the sinking of a great ship. She would take them all down with her. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>The Mistress</i> is everything we've come to love about Tiffany Reisz's writing; flawless, packed with emotion and transcendental. It's quite breathtaking just how effortlessly the prose captures our interest and doesn't let go even long after the last page is fl</span>
  <span id="freeText17935421455497494170" style="display:none"><b>RATING: 4 Forever. Everything. Hearts!! &lt;3</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Søren couldn’t live in a world without Nora. Kingsley couldn’t live in a world without Søren. Her death would be like the sinking of a great ship. She would take them all down with her. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>The Mistress</i> is everything we've come to love about Tiffany Reisz's writing; flawless, packed with emotion and transcendental. It's quite breathtaking just how effortlessly the prose captures our interest and doesn't let go even long after the last page is flipped. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Don’t be afraid,” he whispered against her lips. “This life is nothing but one blink of God’s eyes. He’ll blink again, and we’ll be back together.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I'm going to keep this short, for my sanity. I've made peace with this book, and that's all that matters.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> When he loved, what he loved, who he loved, he loved eternally. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The first 85%: 5+++++++ Hearts. So much raw emotions from all characters. I loved Søren, Kingsley, Nora and Wes's POVs. But what I loved the most is the love these characters have for one another. Søren's for King and Nora. Nora's for Wes and Søren. Simply beautiful. After this, I can say I love Søren, but I love him even more with Kingsley.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “First Samuel 18:1. ‘And it came to pass, when he had made an end of speaking unto Saul, that the soul of Jonathan was knit with the soul of David, and Jonathan loved him as his own soul.’ First Samuel 20:16-17. ‘So Jonathan made a covenant with the house of David, saying, “Let the Lord even require it at the hands of David’s enemies.” And Jonathan caused David to swear again, because he loved him: for he loved as he loved his own soul.’ Second Samual 1:26. ‘I am distressed for thee, my brother Jonathan...thy love to me was wonderful, passing the love of women.”” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />And Kingsley Théophile Boissonneault, this man. WOW. I have never been so soul-deeply entrenched in a male character's emotions as I was with his. I felt his pain, his struggles, and his endless love for Søren; I felt it to my bones. I've said this with the previous books, but I can't write out my feelings when they're so complex. There are no words to describe my infinite love for this broken, utterly beautiful soul. All I can say is, He is loved by me. Always. Forever. With Everything I am. &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3 <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Sometimes the only way to show someone you love them is to let them go. It’s hard, though. It’s so fucking hard.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The last 15%: It's not about what I wanted, it's more I didn't accept it for the characters who've become so endearing to me, changed in a snap. I'll leave it at that. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Love versus love. King, you’re comparing infinities. There is no ‘more’. That’s not how love works. If it’s love, it’s infinite. You can’t count it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This series has been such an emotionally turbulent journey, but I have nothing but words of happiness and joy at finally having been a part of this stunning world of sin, unconventional happenings, and above all, love. Thank you Søren, Kingsley, Nora, Wes, Griff, Michael and Tiffany Reisz for taking me in and making me see a world beyond my own, and making me fall irrevocably in love with that world. For that you have my forever love and gratitude. <i>Many Waters...</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “I know that love is giving yourself to someone else. Giving yourself to someone without losing yourself.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Really looking forward to The White Years!! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Jeg elsker deg, min lille en, Du tilhører mig.” <br />I love you, Little One. You belong to me. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Thank you soooo much to Stephanie for holding my hand through this epic journey, and letting me vent even in the wee hours of the morning. Love you to pieces, woman!! xoxoxo</i><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Posted: February 1, 2017</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_1135744492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135744492" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406624675p2/31339793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135744492?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18270788-the-mistress">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=books-i-d-have-babies-with">books-i-d-have-babies-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=i-trust-feifei">i-trust-feifei</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=im-gonna-need-therapy">im-gonna-need-therapy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=mind-fuck">mind-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=motha-whiplash-emotions">motha-whiplash-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=back-to-paperback">back-to-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=tiffany-reisz-is-godsent">tiffany-reisz-is-godsent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=buddy-recs">buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=smartass-witty-banters">smartass-witty-banters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135744492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5947732618458369079"><b>5 CHECKMATE STARS! ★★★★★</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419409258i/13058575.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"And she said this queen would be two things to me. She would be my heart. And she would be my penance."</i>
</b><br/><br/>After putting down this one, I have given up trying to figure out how Tiffany Reisz's mind works or how she effortlessly keeps stumping me book after book. The last instalment here in the Red Years Quartet left me in an absolute mess because I don't know how to move on after this. In fact, I'm left speechless with how to write a proper review on how amazing this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText5947732618458369079" style="display:none"><b>5 CHECKMATE STARS! ★★★★★</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419409258i/13058575.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"And she said this queen would be two things to me. She would be my heart. And she would be my penance."</i>
</b><br><br>After putting down this one, I have given up trying to figure out how Tiffany Reisz's mind works or how she effortlessly keeps stumping me book after book. The last instalment here in the Red Years Quartet left me in an absolute mess because I don't know how to move on after this. In fact, I'm left speechless with how to write a proper review on how amazing this book/series is. <br><br>I bow down to this lady, I still cannot find the adequate adjective for her godsent writing because it's like nothing I've ever read before. <i>Simply perfection.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404161193ra/10200486.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>This Mistress</b>
</i> surely had the dramatics of a final instalment and can I just say how much <b>I adore the chessplay concept being embedded</b> into this read?! What an absolute genius that is TR being the chessmaster and knowing how to move all her pieces into place which led up right to the ultimate checkmate move. And dare I say, it left so many readers (me included) stumped with one of the most bizarre ending that I did not see coming! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404786203ra/10283286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Admittedly, this was my least favourite instalment (The Prince is still byfar the best!) because of how some of the things panned out and while I would have loved to give this more than 5 stars, there were just some things that left me feeling a little conflicted such as: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>- <b>THAT ENDING.</b> *fumes* I know I sorta expect TR to end this book in an unconventional way but GAH SRSLY GRACE?! Ugh I'm heartbroken to be honest :( I can see how Grace has been given the role of "the rook" (which is one of the most powerful piece on the chessboard) but I really wished that TR didn't grant her that much power that allowed her to have Soren's baby. <br><br>It just came off a little bit out of character for me that Soren would allow himself to go that far with Grace especially when all these years, he would only allow King &amp; Nora to be at that level.<br><br>- <b>Wes and Laila.</b> While I appreciated the addition of Laila in this one, I was kinda baffled by how quickly Wes moved on from Nora. I felt like Laila was just brought into this as a means to an end for Wes to get his HEA. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'm not gonna go full-fledged on this review because all that I needed to say about this series has been mostly said in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1056051057?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">review for The Siren</a>. The Original Sinners series definitely showcases originality, it stretches boundaries and if you allow yourself to be open-minded enough to embrace this read, I promise you that you will find yourself in awe of how a writer can pull off such an amazing feat with this series. Tiffany Reisz does <b>unconventional romance</b> with such elegance and turned it into such a <b>heartfelt read</b> that you cannot help but fall in love with almost every character. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because there is nothing I wouldn’t do to protect you, Eleanor. Nothing I wouldn’t do to help you. And nothing I wouldn’t do to save you. Nothing.”</i>
</blockquote> <br>At this point, I'm still trying to figure out how to get out of this mega book hangover that this series have left me in. I DNF-ed 3 reads after that and it's almost depressing now because I feel like I have lost my purpose in life.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398915050ra/9481997.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5947732618458369079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=tumblr_mao0qrHGdh1ruuuzv_zpsa9271388.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>FUCK FUCK FUCKITY FUCK! It's been twelve hours and I can't compose myself enough to compose a non-ranting review. WTF just happened!<br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=mess_zps722e5b7b.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>Mistress Tiffany, I bow to you! I fear your crazy mind! You are The Queen of Allison mind fucks!<br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=mindfuck_zps88bfafd3.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/621180.gif' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>*Deep breath*Let's get the ramble on....do not proceed if you haven't read up through The Prince as it has spoilers from that book.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=tumblr_mh1s5p9RQ01s446qto1_500_zpsa535f646.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395981ra/763007.gif' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&current=8669081d2f22b2fda849081f340c17b9_zps6f039388.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763008.jpg' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The Mistress, the final installment of The Original Sinners series was composed based on a chess game. I had NO<br/>clue h</span>
  <span id="freeText9169173748846479660" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Book%20funnies/?action=view&amp;current=c632d75db68b6c7821895508bf3f78a3_zpsb45fa3b9.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763005.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_mao0qrHGdh1ruuuzv_zpsa9271388.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395981ra/763006.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>FUCK FUCK FUCKITY FUCK! It's been twelve hours and I can't compose myself enough to compose a non-ranting review. WTF just happened!<br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=mess_zps722e5b7b.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/646179.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Mistress Tiffany, I bow to you! I fear your crazy mind! You are The Queen of Allison mind fucks!<br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=mindfuck_zps88bfafd3.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/621180.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>*Deep breath*Let's get the ramble on....do not proceed if you haven't read up through The Prince as it has spoilers from that book.<br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_mh1s5p9RQ01s446qto1_500_zpsa535f646.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395981ra/763007.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=8669081d2f22b2fda849081f340c17b9_zps6f039388.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763008.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Mistress, the final installment of The Original Sinners series was composed based on a chess game. I had NO<br>clue how to play chess and google was very helpful, as well as (shout out) Amy on Goodreads. It's good to read up on each piece as the characters in the book fit in their placement of the story. <br><br>The White King-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=da80425ee254d6253da8c120503d0680_zpsa8c06999.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763009._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Marie-Laure abducts Nora at the end of The Prince. She's obviously alive and is ready to meet her King again. They think she's dead....they're wrong. She will lure the king to her before taking him.....and the best way to get to the King is to lure him with Nora. <br><br>The White Queen-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=fcb61a772146ac25dbb38b662609a90b_zps4f29c075.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395820i/762504._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nora, abducted by this psycho bitch, is being held captive in Soren's childhood home. She's forced to tell Marie-Laure tale after tale of her history with Kingsley or Soren..... This twisted bitch seems to get off on it. <br><br>The Black Queen-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=938c2ba9fab0422bbadacf5cd5968c5d_zps44a5d40a.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763010._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Marie-Laure has all her pieces in place. She's got his Queen. He will come for her....and she will have him back....her husband back. Dead or alive. <br><br>The Knight-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=b7b57cdb17af7eaa6e7dce8815c66524_zps3862b4ed.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395820i/762503._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wesley can't believe he'd been hit upside the head and Nora taken from his stables. As much as he despises Soren, he makes the call. He has to find her. He loves his Nora. If its the last thing he does, she will be his. He will take her away from all this twisted, sadistic lifestyle.<br> <br>The King-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=9622b6bffd1b92eb36d50fa6da3e67e7_zps3ab1da2d.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395820i/762505._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Kingsley knows the minute he reads the writing in blood on the walls saying "Love thy sister" who's behind the fire in Soren's bed, the fire in Nora's house...and the abduction of Nora. He will get her back safely. He will NOT let her lure Soren. He will protect them both to the death.....but in the end, could he kill his sister?<br><br>The Rook-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=16ca0f11b3a993e990cc06aa7f6f3da4_zps30ac61d2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763011._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Grace reappears in the story while visiting Manhattan while Zachary is in Australia. She's strangley interested in the Eighth Circle. When she meets Soren in person, she's drawn to him like no other man. He's truly almost God-like. Now she knows what Nora finds so addictive. She becomes Soren's sounding board during the hours of waiting.....<br><br>The Pawn-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=cb211556eb54b6e3a43d8638099d66d1_zps28bb9519.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763012._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Laila is Soren's niece visiting from Denmark. A surprise visit Marie-Laure construed to lure her into this sorted game. Beautiful, 18-year old Laila is fiercely loyal to her Uncle Soren and Aunt Elle.<br><br>So, there the set-up. No spoilers here. The book has to be experienced. Any potential spoilers in my ensuring RANT shall be hidden for those who've also succumbed to this mind fuck of a book!<br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=5db8a0e93a967cc7b1c6a75997d43e7c_zps131134b8.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763013.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved how the book was divided into each character (each piece). We begin to see the story unfold and what each person's role was in the end..... We also get great flashbacks to the history between Nora and Kingsley or Nora and Soren via Marie-Laure's curiosity during her captivity. I LOVED Nora's humor through one of the obviously most scary moments of her life. She kept it light and it was laugh out loud funny at times. I seriously don't think I've ever found a heroine as strong as Nora! Marie-Laure....what a raving bitch. I just prayed she would see reason...she'd rethink her actions if not for Soren, but for her brother. <br><br>Wesley, well <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I can't say that I wasn't disappointed in his actions in this book. I've always loved him but knew from the start that those two did not fit together. He could never tame Nora nor should she try to change for his vanilla ways. I get that completely but I was AMAZED he sand-bagged the entire book with Laila, not admitting to her he was engaged to Nora. He was so all-encompassing in love with Nora a few days prior and now he's sitting in a bed chatting it up with Soren's 18-year old niece, conveniently leaving out who he is to Nora. AND THEN TO TAKE HER VIRGINITY SO QUICKLY? WTF? That did not fit his personality to me at all. Maybe a little kiss or something....leave it at that. We can take it from there.....- <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Kingsley- I've vacillated in this series with him. Sometimes I've loved loved loved him but others he kind of rubbed me the wrong way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But when he shows up and that point where he was ready to shoot Nora? Woah? My heart stopped there! I get it....he thought she was going to stab Soren with the dagger but still.... I can say I do love he and Soren's story. It's angsty, fidgety, and those scenes between he and Soren in The Prince were a highlight in the series for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Soren- he is my favorite of all the characters. I've grown to love that tortured soul. In The Siren, I couldn't believe the taboo of incorporating a Catholic priest into a storyline such as this and I proceeded with huge caution. Being a Catholic myself, it seriously tested my ability to hold on.... But Mistress Tiffany strikes again and hooked me! Amazing to me too that she actually taught me things about my faith I had no clue. I cannot stress enough the stellar level of story writing she constructed here. It all falls together. Flawlessly. My one bitch though....omg..... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ what the f&amp;ck was Soren thinking screwing Grace with NO protection? And her getting pregnant? Just one final fuck to our heads, Mistress Tiffany? And what's up with Soren LAUGHING? I didn't get the laugh! So, he's a baby daddy. Obviously Zachary was calling to tell him Fionn was his "blonde" son.... But what's up with the laugh? One final mind f&amp;ck, Tiffany? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Ah, so it ends. Loved the ride. Sad to see it's over. But a great ride nonetheless....<br><br> <a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=partysover_zps7458f61c.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763014.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9169173748846479660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6077700371278830183"><br/><br/><b> Ladies, this is on Net Galley, go ask for a copy. <div id="review_445667238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445667238" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445667238?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=bdsm-kink">bdsm-kink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=smuttastic">smuttastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=gamma-hero">gamma-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=menage">menage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445667238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1312980376292110485">As I sit down here to write this review, I’m almost at a loss for words. There’s something about Tiffany Reisz’s writing that completely transcends the erotic fiction genre and takes me somewhere that no author seems to be able to take me. It’s almost like sub-space – I find myself in a dream-like trance when I read her work. A lot of the time I don’t want to continue, a little afraid of what is coming next, but I am utterly compelled, completely entranced by the story and fully invested in the </span>
  <span id="freeText1312980376292110485" style="display:none">As I sit down here to write this review, I’m almost at a loss for words. There’s something about Tiffany Reisz’s writing that completely transcends the erotic fiction genre and takes me somewhere that no author seems to be able to take me. It’s almost like sub-space – I find myself in a dream-like trance when I read her work. A lot of the time I don’t want to continue, a little afraid of what is coming next, but I am utterly compelled, completely entranced by the story and fully invested in the characters who have become so real to me over the course of The Original Sinners series.<br /><br />We rejoin our Kinksters right where we left them at the end of The Prince. Nora has been kidnapped and is being held in bonds, for once against her will, and having to make like Scheherazade to save her life. She’s in the worst predicament of her life, and she’s been in a few, let’s face it, and now it seems that the only person that can save her is herself. The seemingly unflappable, icy-calm Søren is as close to losing his cool as we are ever likely to see him and Kingsley has to resort to desperate measures to prevent him from doing something foolish to endanger both himself and Nora out of sheer despair. Wes is also completely lost – he can do nothing apart from turn to Kingsley and Søren for help, despite his reservations about them and their lifestyle.<br /><br />I don’t want to give away the plot – I really want for you all to experience it the way I did. I absolutely didn’t know what was coming next the whole time I was reading. With any other author, I think it’s safe to say that you’d have fairly high expectations of a rescue and a comforting and traditional Happy Ever After but this is Queen Tiff and you have to learn to expected the unexpected when you read her. She is a Master Storyteller, or should that be Mistress Storyteller, and it pays to remember that she is never going to wrap everything up neatly with a bow on top – she’s always going to boldly go where no erotic fiction writer has ever gone before should she choose to and, believe me, she chooses to. There was one chapter that ended with two characters kneeling facing one another and I had to close my Kindle and walk away – I had to force myself to do this because I was so afraid to continue. This is a moment of absolute crisis in the story and all appears lost and, I was so engrossed in the story and the characters, that I was terrified to carry on, fearing what on earth Tiff may unleash upon us!<br /><br /><br />I feel deeper in love with all the characters in The Mistress. Kingsley – je t’adore comme toujours but now there is a special place in my heart reserved solely for Søren. I’ve come on a long journey with Søren since I first met him in Seven Day Loan when I really didn’t like him but throughout The Siren, The Angel and The Prince I’ve grown to love him and to finally begin to understand this brilliant, complex man. To know Søren is to submit to Søren. Even as just mere words on a page, his power and authority emanate in intense waves right out to me as a reader and I have the urge to kneel before him, He’s not an easy character to know or like – after all he’s a hard-core sadist AND a catholic priest, not the most compatible of bed-fellows but now I feel that I have come full-circle with him and am now in awe of his incredible intelligence, his compassion and his powerful demeanour. Never before has a fictional sadist seemed so complex and multi-dimensional to me.<br /><br />Tiff has created these characters and drip-fed their stories both past and present to us during the novels of the series and I’ve grown to love and understand them all. The writing is, as always, sublime, enthralling and totally captivating. Despite this particular story being paced quite slowly with plenty of flashbacks, it still managed to be edge of the seat reading for me. I was rapt, sometimes fearful to continue, but completely unable to push this one far from my thoughts when I wasn’t reading it. Nora, Søren, Kingsley and Wes have all come alive in my imagination as I’ve endured their triumphs and disasters with them. The whole series feels like it was meticulously planned – Tiff clearly knows her characters intimately, it feels almost as if they’re stood in front of her telling her their stories as she writes.<br /><br />Despite everyone’s morals being very far removed from the acceptable norm, there is actually great nobility and undying loyalty to be found here. There is a distinct lack of monogamy but infidelity is too harsh a word for the acceptance and understanding that passes between them all. I think you’d have to look hard to find a greater and deeper love than you’ll find here. Kingsley loves Søren, Søren loves Kingsley and Nora, Nora loves Søren and Wes loves Nora and all of this is kind of intoxicating to read. There’s profound honesty, trust and a soul-deep understanding of one another. We also get to catch up with Daniel and Grace – two characters from past novels.<br /><br />I think I am still enamoured most of all with Kingsley Edge – that wicked Frenchman who dresses as a 19th century dandy but it’s easy to forget that beneath the facade beats the heart of a ruthless assassin and he is not going to take kindly to one of his own being placed in mortal danger, whoever the perpetrator may be. He still makes my panties spontaneously combust! There’s a glimmer of happiness on the horizon for Kingsley, for a future that he could never have forseen for himself if only he can survive Nora’s current predicament. Nora is, as ever, arrogant, cocky, dangerous and captivating, even in her darkest moment. I suspect there’s quite a bit of Tiffany Reisz in Nora – as a character, she’s a tour de force, very richly drawn and so engaging.<br /><br />Wes is the one character. I’ve been least invested in throughout the whole series. I do like him but have always considered him to be out of his depth, almost child-like but he’s about to be bitchslapped into manhood in this one as he learns as much about what he wants as what he doesn’t want especially from Nora, Kingsley and Søren. I’ve never been Team Wes, even when I disliked Søren but I am happy with how his storyline panned out in The Mistress.<br /><br />So, to sum it up – despite everything that goes on here, this is ultimately a story of the most sincere love you are ever likely to see. It’s smart, witty, super sharp and absolutely compelling and captivating. I bow down at Queen Tiff’s feet – she can seemingly do no wrong.<br /><br /><br />5 stunning stars<br /><br /> <i>For more reviews, please visit <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a> or visit us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</i></span>

  <span id="freeText7370113872256535520" style="display:none"><b>♦ 4.5 STARS. ♦</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402084i/781302._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
