<span id="freeTextContainer15120747369888912644"><b><br/><u>Full review posted 03.08.2013.</u><br/><br/>* * * This book was beautiful, sad, sweet, scary, mysterious, heartbreaking, kinky, happy, intense and all kinds of orgasmic. Ginormous 5 stars from me :-D.* * *<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399947ra/774481.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></b><br/>Dear Lord, Tiffany Reisz outdid herself this time. This is my favorite book in these series so far. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>If you haven't read at least the first book in the series, do not read further.</b>
</i><br/><br/>In her previous books there were characters I liked and characters I loved, in this one, I fell head over heals with ALL of th</span>
  <span id="freeText15120747369888912644" style="display:none"><b><br><u>Full review posted 03.08.2013.</u><br><br>* * * This book was beautiful, sad, sweet, scary, mysterious, heartbreaking, kinky, happy, intense and all kinds of orgasmic. Ginormous 5 stars from me :-D.* * *<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399947ra/774481.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b><br>Dear Lord, Tiffany Reisz outdid herself this time. This is my favorite book in these series so far. <br><br><i>
  <b>If you haven't read at least the first book in the series, do not read further.</b>
</i><br><br>In her previous books there were characters I liked and characters I loved, in this one, I fell head over heals with ALL of them.<br><br><b>
  <u>Nora:</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774482.jpg" width="400" height="650" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If you've read previous book, you know what happened to Nora. She found herself in a very bad situation. I think I've said that already, in one of my updates, but I'm going to say again: Nora is the worse captive ever :-D. She was really trying her captors patients. The woman has balls the size of two watermelons :-D. Even though most of the time she was cracking jokes and insulting her captor, you could see that she was scared shitless. It was nice to see the softer side of Nora. I fell in love with her even more.<br><br><b>
  <u>Wesley:</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774483.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Poor Wesley, I really felt bad for him. Poor kid is hopelessly in love with Nora. When she went missing he was loosing his mind, hyperventilating, his blood sugar was through the roof, he didn't know what to do with himself. I loved his conversations with Kingsley and Søren. Loved it even more when he finally buried the hatched with those to. He wanted to hate them so badly, but how could he, after he got to know them better.<br>But I did have a problem with him towards the end. I won't take any stars because of it, because I loved the story as a whole, but my god, Wes. WTF, dude??!! I see Kingsley's and Søren's stories have rubbed off on you ;-). He was the only good/vanilla guy in the series, and now... Apparently when Nora took his virginity his soul fallowed :-D. Tsk, tsk, Wesley.<br><br><b>
  <u>Griffin:</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774484.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There wasn't much of Griffin in this book, but Tiffany Reisz made sure that as little appearance as he had, that he won't be forgotten :-D. It was nice to see that him and his little angel are still going strong.<br><br><b>
  <u>Kingsley:</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774485.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I can't fan-girl about him enough. I wish Kingsley was a real person :-D. I love you, you french f@cker :-). <br>In The Mistress we got to read more about his relationship with Søren and Nora. As kinky and kind of f@cked up as their relationship is, it is also beautiful and even sweet. Tiffany Reisz managed to convince me that their love triangle can and will work. Which is mind-blowing, because I would've never imagined something like that working in a real life. That just shows how brilliant Reisz is.<br>I loved, LOVED, Kingsley's encounters with Wesley and Nora. <br><br><b>
  <u>Søren:</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774486.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Søren's character is the hardest one for me to describe. I'm lost for words. What kind of kinky f@ckery is cooking in Tiffany's Reisz head? How in a world did she came up with him?<br>We got to read a lot about Søren in this book. He tells these bizarre stories with such calm and ease , it freaks me out :-S. Søren is out of this world. I have a hard time imagining someone like him existing in real life. There is no way a person could be so... dark and twisted and so good and loving at the same time. He was a definitely a martyr in this book. He was the one that turned the other cheek. How suiting :-). I loved his struggles and his week moments. I felt his loss and his pain. <br>Dear Lord, the scene towards the end, with Nora kneeling in front of him, the things they said to each other, was heartbreaking and oh-so beautiful. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399947i/774487.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The way he quotes bible, the advices he gives to other, are just... uh. I love him, that's all I can say :-D.<br><br>But here is the freakiest thing about this book: after reading this book I actually wanted to go to church. My god, of all the books in the world, this kinky f@ckery got me thinking about god. I guess Søren spoke my language :-D. <br><br>As for the ending. WTF? I still can't wrap my head around it. Why was Søren laughing? What did Zachary told him? I have my theory, but I'm not sure I want to be right about it. Ugh!!! Tiffany, hurry with the next book, will ya ;-).<br><br>I won't comment on writing, character development or the plot, it's the fourth installment in the series and if you've read at least one book in the series, you know that no words are necessary, it's superb.io</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer554685224163425410"><br/>OK it is NOT my day... I tried to do a review 2x and both time I closed it by accident I physically can't do it anymore!<br/><br/>But I will say it is one of the best books (if you ignore that last few % of it)<br/><br/><b>Bravo, Tiffany Reisz</b> for being such a clever book Dominatrix.   <span id="freeText554685224163425410" style="display:none"><br>OK it is NOT my day... I tried to do a review 2x and both time I closed it by accident I physically can't do it anymore!<br><br>But I will say it is one of the best books (if you ignore that last few % of it)<br><br><b>Bravo, Tiffany Reisz</b> for being such a clever book Dominatrix. If you know chess this book will be 2x as interesting I think but even being ignorant in the art of Chess I loved every second of it (again... ignoring those last few % at the end). Therefore I'm going to go with a 5star rating... but losing all the ++++++++ that I was adding on every time I highlighted in the book... just in case you wondering Kindle Highlights informs me it was 34 times.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Kingsley knelt down at Søren’s feet and rested his hand on Nora’s hip right under where she’d been kicked. They’d both been wounded for their sins, and both found their healing at his feet and in his arms.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><b>
  <u> My Soren </u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399279i/772467._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>A world without Nora Sutherlin was a world without Søren. If the priest lost his Little One, especially if her death happened because of something Søren had done, no matter how inadvertently, it would mean his destruction. Søren couldn’t live in a world without Nora. Kingsley couldn’t live in a world without Søren. Her death would be like the sinking of a great ship. She would take them all down with her.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><b>
  <u> My Nora </u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399279i/772468._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>It seems you have a pathological fear of making any definitive choices in your life. You flit from man to man and never completely commit to anyone. Once you make a decision, you don’t stick with it. You promised yourself to him,” she said, pointing at Søren, “and then you left him. You had another man in your life and you sent him away. Then you went back to my husband but you didn’t stay with him, either. Back and forth, back and forth.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <u> My Kingsley </u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399279i/772469._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399279i/772470._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Money bought nothing in Kingsley’s world but a key to the front door. Once inside, they built their own kingdoms. Dominants with boring day jobs earned respect with the power they created out of their own dignity and desires. Exquisite submissives— male and female— who laid themselves out on the altar of sacrifice and sexuality in order to find themselves at someone else’s feet. Wesley always accused the people of her world of putting on costumes and playing dress-up. He had no idea that the suits and the ties and the beige pumps and navy slacks her people wore during the day were the real costumes that they shed when they came out after dark.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379797348i/630503._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Know that love is giving yourself to someone else. Giving yourself to someone without losing yourself.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="554685224163425410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_679240450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679240450" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580475762p2/12928663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679240450?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=bdsm">bdsm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=feeeeels">feeeeels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679240450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17656333689557097296"><i>
  <b>“Bitch, please—I’m kinkier than he is.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430846i/864018.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>The Mistress</i> picks up just minutes after the huge cliffhanger we’re left with after <i>The Prince</i>. Nora has been taken <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[yes, by Kinglsey’s “dead” sister, Marie-Laure <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and everyone is trying to piece together what happened, where she is, and who took her. <br/><br/>There are a few new and old faces that pop up in this one. First we have Grace, Zach’s wife. Her presence in the story was odd to me at first, we haven’t seen her for the last </span>
  <span id="freeText17656333689557097296" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Bitch, please—I’m kinkier than he is.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430846i/864018.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Mistress</i> picks up just minutes after the huge cliffhanger we’re left with after <i>The Prince</i>. Nora has been taken <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[yes, by Kinglsey’s “dead” sister, Marie-Laure <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and everyone is trying to piece together what happened, where she is, and who took her. <br><br>There are a few new and old faces that pop up in this one. First we have Grace, Zach’s wife. Her presence in the story was odd to me at first, we haven’t seen her for the last two books, why now? As it went on I got more used to her being there and it was nice to have another woman in the story since Nora is always surrounded by men. Not entirely sold on them being friends, but this is an odd bunch so whatevs. Søren’s niece Laila is also is a key player. She has information about Nora’s kidnapper and I really liked how her character evolved in the short time we see her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I loved that her and Wesley end up together. I called it from their first interaction and thought it seemed very obvious, but I was surprisingly alright with it. They were sweet and I’m glad that Wesley removed himself from everything and realized he needed a good ol’ vanilla girl. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>This book was full of powerful moments. There were several small interactions between various characters that had me hanging on every word. Wesley &amp; Kinglsey, Søren &amp; Wesley, Kingsley &amp; Nora, Soren &amp; Nøra, etc. I find these characters so fascinating and when we get to see them hash it out over issues I’m dying to hear about, it’s priceless. I have been so conflicted about how I wanted this series to end. Who I wanted with whom, who I think will end up happy, who I think will be heartbroken, and I have to say I was pleasantly surprised. Not only were my feelings cemented for certain characters, but I also got this sense of contentment about where things were heading. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Love versus love. King, you’re comparing infinities. There is no ‘more.’ That’s not how love works. If it’s love, it’s infinite. You can’t count it…” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>While Nora is held captive there are a lot of flashbacks to key scenes. While some of those moments were favorites out of the whole series, it started to feel like flashback after flashback with no real meat in the present (with her). I liked the premise of Nora being in trouble and the kinksters of The 8th Circle banding together to save her but it didn’t live up to my expectations. As much as I am a die-hard fan of this series, this book didn’t enrapture me like the previous did. It is still amazingly written, so smart, and made me feel so deep for these characters I already love, but it just wasn’t as good for me. <br><br>And the ending, I was pretty satisfied with everything leading up to it. I was feeling content and a little surprised <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that everyone was getting a HEA <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and then my feelings changed a bit. If you peeps saw my status at the end you know… I literally shouted, “What the fuck!?” then I burst out laughing. I felt like a straight up crazy person. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The freaking bomb dropped at the end about Søren being the baby daddy was *smh* I don’t even know what to say. I’m not mad at Søren, I’m not mad at Grace, I don’t really think Nora would be upset. That’s not my issue. I think it was just unneeded. It felt like shock value for shock value sake. It ultimately left me feeling confused about why that was even done. Being different or shocking just isn’t a good enough reason for me. *shrugs* lol Other than that last part I was digging how everything had played out. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Although I loved <i>The Angel</i> and <i>The Prince</i> more and this one has left me feeling the most conflicted (I am still a bit confused about my rating) that in no way changes my feelings about this series as a whole. It is one of my <b>favorite series ever</b>. I love that I never know how to categorize it or explain it to people. It’s different, it’s untraditional, and it transcends boundaries. I am ridiculously attached to these characters (Kingsley!! Who am I kidding? I love EVERYONE!!) and the writing is enthralling, amazing, and beautiful. <br><br>I am counting down the days until <i>The Priest</i>. Thank <s>Søren</s> god we are getting FOUR MORE books! Yay! <br><br><i><b>“I knelt at his feet because I felt like that’s where I belonged. And no, not because I was so unworthy of him, but because he was so utterly worthy of my devotion.”<br><br>4 stars. </b> Maybe 4.5?</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17656333689557097296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ysd1VUoWOSSPRhSW67aX7kDNzXcUuC97zfkAvOK6b8r8fbPFUZ2mf9E5YjCYYIbOd8pl9/ZAdGHFYCn9b4ArAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IASLmjWBskuy7WgRQ5SviRHRut8UxAHkBnRg1WInM/kWvk0KLgotEOySHrcwQr6pJtYSX/Y8Wv4O7UmU7x13Mg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2373361090753706786">Tiffany Reisz is the <i>USA Today</i>-bestselling author of the Romance Writers of America RITA®-winning Original Sinners series from Harlequin's Mira Books.<br/><br/>Born in Owensboro, Kentucky, Tiffany graduated from Centre College with a B.A. in English. She began her writing career while a student at Wilmore, Kentucky's Asbury Theological Seminary. After leaving seminary to focus on her fiction, she wrote <i>The </i></span>
  <span id="freeText2373361090753706786" style="display:none">Tiffany Reisz is the <i>USA Today</i>-bestselling author of the Romance Writers of America RITA®-winning Original Sinners series from Harlequin's Mira Books.<br /><br />Born in Owensboro, Kentucky, Tiffany graduated from Centre College with a B.A. in English. She began her writing career while a student at Wilmore, Kentucky's Asbury Theological Seminary. After leaving seminary to focus on her fiction, she wrote <i>The Siren</i>, which has sold more than half a million copies worldwide. <br /><br />Tiffany also writes mainstream women's suspense fiction, including <i>The Bourbon Thief</i> (winner of the <i>RT Book Reviews</i> Seal of Excellence Award) and the RITA®-nominated <i>The Night Mark</i>.<br /><br />Her erotic fantasy <i>The Red</i>—self-published under the banner 8th Circle Press—was named an <i>NPR</i> Best Book of the Year and a Goodreads Best Romance of the Month. It also received a coveted starred review from <i>Library Journal</i>. <br /><br />Tiffany lives in Louisville, Kentucky with her husband, author Andrew Shaffer, and two cats. The cats are not writers. </span>
